 assert an ordinary quasi-isomorphism.
\end{enumerate}

\smallskip\noindent\emph{Scope.}
The Koszul hypothesis is essential: for simple admissible affine
quotients and minimal-model Virasoro/W-algebras the PBW/Shapovalov
argument is unavailable, the square-zero bar spectral sequence can
carry extra higher-differential data, and this chapter does
\emph{not} claim that the counit $\psi$ is a quasi-isomorphism there
\textup{(}see Remark~\ref{rem:sl2-admissible}
and~\ref{rem:virasoro-module-koszul-minimal}\textup{)}. In those regimes one must work
with the completed correspondence of
Corollary~\ref{cor:bar-cobar-inverse} and the intrinsic
coderived/contraderived bar-coalgebra comparison of
Theorems~\ref{thm:positselski-chiral-proved}
and~\ref{thm:full-derived-module-equiv-proved}; this theorem
asserts the coderived statement of~(2), and isolates in~(4) the extra
input needed to recover an ordinary quasi-isomorphism there.
\end{theorem}


\begin{example}[Admissible-level failure of bar-cobar inversion]
\label{ex:admissible-sl2-failure}
\index{admissible level!bar-cobar inversion failure}
\index{bar-cobar inversion!admissible-level counterexample}
Consider $L_{-1/2}(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$, the simple affine vertex algebra
at the admissible level $k = -1/2$ for $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$
(here $h^\vee = 2$, so $k + h^\vee = 3/2$; the admissible
parametrization is $k = -h^\vee + p/q$ with $p = 3$, $q = 2$).
This algebra is excluded from the Koszul locus of
Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi}; the concrete mechanism by
which bar-cobar inversion fails is the following.

\emph{Singular vector in the bar-relevant range.}
The vacuum Verma module $M(k\Lambda_0)$ at $k = -1/2$ has a
singular vector at conformal weight $(p-1)q = 2 \cdot 2 = 4$,
produced by the Kac--Kazhdan root $\beta_{q,-} = q\delta - \alpha$
at KK value $j = p - 1 = 2$
(Kac--Wakimoto~\cite{KW88};
cf.\ Remark~\ref{rem:sl2-admissible}).
Since the strong generators $J^+, J^0, J^-$ of
$\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$ all have conformal weight~$1$, the
bar-relevant range begins at conformal weight~$2$
(bar degree~$\geq 2$), so this singular vector at weight~$4$
lies squarely in the bar-relevant range.

\emph{Effect on the bar complex.}
Passing to the simple quotient $L_{-1/2}(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ kills
this singular vector, introducing an extra relation not present at
generic level. In the bar complex
$\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(L_{-1/2}(\mathfrak{sl}_2))$,
this relation produces bar cohomology off the Koszul diagonal:
at generic level $k$, the Koszul property concentrates
$H^n(\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)))$ in internal
degree~$n$ (the ``Koszul diagonal''), whereas at $k = -1/2$ the
null vector at weight~$4$ generates an off-diagonal class that
persists in $H^\bullet(\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}})$.

\emph{Spectral sequence non-collapse.}
The square-zero bar-cobar spectral sequence of
Theorems~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-spectral-sequence}
and~\ref{thm:spectral-sequence-collapse} relies on
Koszul-diagonal concentration for its $E_2$ collapse. The
off-diagonal class at weight~$4$ supports a non-trivial higher
differential, so the spectral sequence does not collapse at $E_2$.
The counit
$\psi\colon \Omega^{\mathrm{ch}}(\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(L_{-1/2}(\mathfrak{sl}_2)))
\to L_{-1/2}(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$
fails to be a quasi-isomorphism: the surviving off-diagonal class
generates a non-trivial extension in
$\Omega^{\mathrm{ch}}(\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(L_{-1/2}(\mathfrak{sl}_2)))$
that has no preimage in $L_{-1/2}(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$.

\emph{Consistency with the Koszul-locus hypothesis.}
At generic level, the vacuum Verma module
$M(k\Lambda_0)$ has no singular vectors in the bar-relevant range,
$H^\bullet(\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2)))$ is
concentrated on the Koszul diagonal, and
Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi} applies. The admissible
level $k = -1/2$ lies outside the Koszul locus because the
representation category
$\mathrm{KL}_{-1/2}(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$
(Arakawa~\cite{Arakawa17, Arakawa2016RationalAdmissible}) is a
non-semisimple finite tensor category whose singular vectors
obstruct the diagonal concentration.
For the critical-level analogue $k = -h^\vee = -2$, the
Feigin--Frenkel center~\cite{Feigin-Frenkel} causes an even more
dramatic failure: the center of
$V_{-2}(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ jumps in dimension and the bar complex
acquires infinitely many off-diagonal classes.
\end{example}

\begin{remark}[$2$-Koszulness at admissible level; \ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{rem:admissible-2-koszul}%
\index{2-Koszul!admissible level}%
\index{admissible level!2-Koszul}%
The preceding example shows that $L_{-1/2}(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ fails
classical Koszulness: bar cohomology
$H^*(\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(L_{-1/2}(\mathfrak{sl}_2)))$ is not
concentrated in degree~$1$. The off-diagonal class produced by the
singular vector at conformal weight~$4$ lives in bar degree~$2$.
A stronger expectation is that the bar cohomology is concentrated in
degrees $\{1, 2\}$, making $L_{-1/2}(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ a
\emph{$2$-Koszul} (or \emph{$N$-Koszul} with $N = 2$) chiral algebra
in the sense of Berger~\cite{Berger01}:
the square-zero bar-cobar spectral sequence
\textup{(}Theorems~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-spectral-sequence}
and~\ref{thm:spectral-sequence-collapse}\textup{)} collapses at a
finite page~$E_N$ rather than at~$E_2$.

This is consistent with the representation-theoretic structure.
The category $\mathrm{KL}_{-1/2}(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ has exactly two
simple objects (vacuum and one non-vacuum admissible module), and the
extension algebra between them is generated in degrees~$1$ and~$2$
with relations in degree~$3$; the $N$-Koszul pattern
$H^n(\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}) = 0$ for $n \geq 3$ would then follow
from the absence of higher singular vectors in the bar-relevant range
beyond the weight-$4$ vector identified above.
If confirmed, this places admissible-level algebras in a hierarchy:
classical Koszul (generic level, $E_2$ collapse) $\subset$
$N$-Koszul (admissible level, $E_N$ collapse) $\subset$
non-Koszul (critical level, no finite collapse).
\end{remark}

\begin{proof}[Dependency-closed proof]
We verify each numbered clause by previously established results in
this chapter and in the coderived appendix.
\begin{enumerate}[label=(D\arabic*)]
\item \emph{Strict Koszul lane.}
The genus-$0$ quasi-isomorphism is proved independently by
Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-nilpotency-complete} and
Theorem~\ref{thm:chiral-koszul-duality};
equivalently, it is the implication
\ref{ftm:koszul}$\Rightarrow$\ref{ftm:counit} of
the fundamental theorem of chiral twisting morphisms
(Theorem~\ref{thm:fundamental-twisting-morphisms}).
Under the higher-genus hypotheses of
Theorem~\ref{thm:higher-genus-inversion}, the genus-$g$ components
$\psi_g$ for $g \geq 1$ are quasi-isomorphisms by induction on genus,
and Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-graded-convergence} supplies the completed
series statement.

\item \emph{Coderived off-Koszul lane.}
Theorem~\ref{thm:off-koszul-ran-inversion} proves that the
factorization counit $\psi_X$ is an isomorphism in the coderived
category for every complete augmented input with finite-dimensional
graded bar pieces. Its proof is independent of
Theorem~\ref{thm:higher-genus-inversion}: it identifies the cone of
$\psi_X$ as coacyclic by stratified Positselski inversion and the
Verdier-quotient criterion for
$D^{\mathrm{co}}(\barB\text{-}\mathrm{CoFact})$.

\item \emph{Coderived bar-degree filtration.}
On the strict square-zero surface, existence and collapse are exactly
Theorems~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-spectral-sequence}
and~\ref{thm:spectral-sequence-collapse}. On the curved surface,
Proposition~\ref{prop:coderived-bar-degree-spectral-sequence}
replaces ordinary abutment by coacyclicity of the cone: the
associated-graded $E_1$ page is strict because the curvature term lies
in positive filtration.

\item \emph{Promotion lane.}
If $\kappa(\mathcal{A}) = 0$, then the curved differential becomes
square-zero, so Theorem~\ref{thm:conilpotent-reduction} identifies the
coderived and ordinary derived categories and the coderived
equivalence of~(D2) is an ordinary quasi-isomorphism. More generally,
any class~$G/L$ collapse input for the coderived bar-degree spectral
sequence turns coacyclicity of the cone into acyclicity, hence into an
ordinary quasi-isomorphism. This is the exact extra hypothesis isolated
in clause~(4).
\end{enumerate}
Combining (D1)--(D4) gives the strongest proved package stated in the
theorem.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Alternative proof via formality]
\label{rem:bar-cobar-inversion-alt-formality}
The strict Koszul lane of
Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi} admits a second proof that
bypasses Theorems~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-spectral-sequence}
and~\ref{thm:spectral-sequence-collapse}. The point is to replace the
spectral-sequence argument by the deformation problem controlled by the
bar coalgebra. Write
\[
\psi \colon \Omega(\barB(\cA)) \longrightarrow \cA
\]
for the counit. After passing to the PBW-associated graded quadratic
model, one is working in the formal neighborhood governed by the
quadratic closure
\[
\cA^i = H^*(\barB(\cA)),
\]
and the homotopy transfer theorem
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:htt}}\textup{)} supplies maps
\[
\cA \;\underset{\psi}{\overset{i}{\rightleftarrows}}\;
\Omega(\barB(\cA))
\]
with $\psi i = \id$ and $i\psi \sim \id$ on the tangent complex of the
bar-cobar deformation problem. In Keller's deformation-theoretic
language, this identifies the formal moduli problem of
$\Omega(\barB(\cA))$ with the one controlled by the transferred
$A_\infty$-structure on~$\cA^i$; on the Koszul locus, PBW
concentration says that this tangent complex is already governed by the
quadratic closure.

The remaining step is formality of the transferred
$A_\infty$-structure on~$\cA^i$. The $\E_2$-formality map realized by
Kontsevich-type configuration-space integrals on
Fulton--MacPherson models
\textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:en-formality}}\textup{)},
and the fiberwise identification of transferred higher operations with
the corresponding FM-stratum operations
\textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:shadow-formality-low-degree}}\textup{)}.
identify the higher $m_n$ with the FM formality obstructions.
Theorem~\ref{thm:ainfty-koszul-characterization} then says that on the
Koszul locus these obstructions vanish, so the transferred
$A_\infty$-structure on~$\cA^i$ is formal. Keller's classicality
theorem for formal $A_\infty$-algebras \cite{Keller01} upgrades the
tangent-level retract to an $A_\infty$ quasi-isomorphism. Applying
$\Omega$ gives
\[
\Omega(\barB(\cA))
\;\simeq\;
\Omega(\cA^i)
\xrightarrow{\sim}
\cA,
\]
where the last quasi-isomorphism is the twisting-morphism/Koszul-duality
identification of
Theorem~\ref{thm:fundamental-twisting-morphisms}
\textup{(}equivalently, Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:chiral-koszul-duality}}
on the quadratic lane\textup{)}. This recovers clause~\textup{(1)}.

Off the Koszul locus the same deformation-retract package survives
after passing to filtered curved models. The transfer data respects
the bar-degree filtration, and the curvature term lies in positive
filtration, so the associated graded retract is strict.
Proposition~\ref{prop:coderived-bar-degree-spectral-sequence} then
identifies the cone of the factorization counit as coacyclic, and
Theorem~\ref{thm:off-koszul-ran-inversion} recovers the coderived
statement of clause~\textup{(2)}. This does not remove the extra
hypothesis in clause~\textup{(4)}: promotion from coderived
equivalence to an ordinary quasi-isomorphism still requires the same
collapse input, or the flat case $\kappa(\cA)=0$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Research remark: the Koszul locus and the off-locus obstruction]
\label{rem:koszul-locus-off-locus-obstruction}
\index{Koszul locus!off-locus obstruction}
\index{bar-cobar inversion!off-locus obstruction}
The phrase ``Koszul locus'' in
Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi} has a precise
genus-$0$ meaning: it is the full subcategory
$\operatorname{Kosz}(X)$ of Definition~\ref{def:koszul-locus}.
Equivalently, $\cA \in \operatorname{Kosz}(X)$ if and only if the
genus-$0$ counit
\[
\Omega_X(\barB_X(\cA)) \longrightarrow \cA
\]
is a quasi-isomorphism; if and only if the PBW/bar spectral sequence
collapses at~$E_2$; if and only if
$H^*(\barB_X(\cA))$ is concentrated on the Koszul diagonal
\textup{(}bar degree equal to internal degree, or after the
reindexing used in
Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-spectral-sequence},
concentrated in bar degree~$1$\textup{)}. For a quadratic
$A_\infty$ model this recovers the classical Priddy/BGS criterion:
the bar cohomology is concentrated in weight~$1$.

The obstruction off the locus is equally concrete: the first
off-diagonal bar class. Once $H^*(\barB_X(\cA))$ acquires a class in
bidegree $(p,q)$ with $q \neq 0$ after the standard reindexing, the
strict square-zero proof loses diagonal concentration, higher
differentials need not vanish, and the cone of the counit can stop
being acyclic in the ordinary derived category. In the quotient
examples already isolated in the manuscript, this class is created by
a null-vector ideal or a non-flat PBW degeneration: singular vectors
enter the bar-relevant range, or composite relations survive in bar
degree $\geq 2$, so the PBW collapse no longer forces strict
inversion.

What survives off the locus is unconditional and already proved:
clause~\textup{(2)} of
Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi} gives a coderived
coacyclic-equivalence for every complete augmented input with
finite-dimensional graded bar pieces. The natural enlargement of
$\operatorname{Kosz}(X)$ is therefore not the whole moduli stack of
chiral algebras, but a derived Koszul locus: the full substack on
which the coderived cone is still detected by ordinary cohomology.
Conjecture~\ref{conj:koszul-wall-associated-variety} formulates this
derived wall. The proved upgrade is narrower: promotion from coderived
equivalence back to a genuine quasi-isomorphism holds on the collapse
loci singled out in clause~\textup{(4)}, including the flat case
$\kappa(\cA)=0$ and any family for which the coderived bar-degree
spectral sequence degenerates to ordinary cohomology.

From this viewpoint, the restrictive surface is not the standard
universal landscape but its pathological quotient boundary. Freely
strongly generated or generic-level families are designed to stay on
the locus: Heisenberg, universal affine $V_k(\fg)$, generic Virasoro,
and the principal $\cW$-families enter through PBW-flat models. The
genuine candidates for leaving the locus are quotient algebras with
null-vector ideals in the bar-relevant range, minimal-model
quotients, higher-rank admissible simple quotients, and other
non-flat or non-freely-generated degenerations. Even there the
coderived comparison remains available; what fails is only the
promotion from coacyclicity to an ordinary quasi-isomorphism.
\end{remark}

\begin{conjecture}[Derived Koszul wall; \ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:koszul-wall-associated-variety}
\index{Koszul locus!derived wall}
\index{associated variety!Koszul wall}
Let $\mathrm{ChAlg}^{\mathrm{aug}}$ be the derived moduli stack of
augmented chiral algebras, and let
\[
\mathrm{Kos}
:=
\left\{
\cA \in \mathrm{ChAlg}^{\mathrm{aug}}
\;\middle|\;
\Omegach\bigl(\barBch(\cA)\bigr) \xrightarrow{\sim} \cA
\right\}
\]
be the bar-cobar inversion locus of
Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi}. Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \textup{(Derived openness)}
 $\mathrm{Kos}$ is an open derived substack of
 $\mathrm{ChAlg}^{\mathrm{aug}}$. Equivalently, for every
 $[\cA] \in \mathrm{Kos}$, the formal completion
 $\widehat{\mathrm{ChAlg}^{\mathrm{aug}}}_{[\cA]}$ is contained in
 $\mathrm{Kos}$, so every derived square-zero deformation of~$\cA$
 still satisfies bar-cobar inversion.
\item \textup{(PBW wall stratification)}
 The complement
 $\mathrm{ChAlg}^{\mathrm{aug}} \setminus \mathrm{Kos}$ is a
 divisor-like wall, but it is not in general of pure codimension~$1$.
 It carries a canonical stratification by the first failure of PBW
 concentration: a point lies in the stratum
 $\mathfrak{W}_{r,w}$ when the bar spectral sequence first acquires
 off-diagonal bar cohomology, equivalently the first nonzero higher
 differential obstructing $E_2$-collapse, on page~$r$ and conformal
 weight~$w$.
\item \textup{(Admissible boundary)}
 The first affine-admissible boundary model is the
 $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$ family at level $k=-1/2$. In the
 passage from the universal algebra
 $V_{-1/2}(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ to its admissible quotient, the
 associated variety in the sense of Arakawa is expected to jump from
 the full nilpotent cone to the closure of a proper orbit; at that
 same boundary one expects new off-diagonal bar classes and the
 failure of PBW concentration. Compare Arakawa's admissible and
 associated-variety package
 \cite{Arakawa2005Duke,Ara12,Arakawa2015ICM,Arakawa2016RationalAdmissible}.
\item \textup{(Singular-support control)}
 More generally, if $X_\cA$ denotes the associated variety of~$\cA$,
 then the Koszul wall is controlled by the singular-support condition
 on~$X_\cA$: the wall is cut out by the failure of the singular
 support to remain the reduced conormal lift of~$X_\cA$, and its
 strata are indexed by the excess microlocal components that appear
 above the singular locus.
\end{enumerate}
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[Relation to the fundamental theorem \texorpdfstring{$\mathrm{A}_0$}{A_0}]
\label{rem:inversion-vs-fundamental}
At genus~$0$, Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi} is a
consequence of the fundamental theorem of chiral twisting morphisms
(Theorem~\ref{thm:fundamental-twisting-morphisms}):
the counit $\Omega_X(\bar{B}_X(\cA)) \to \cA$ being a
quasi-isomorphism is one of the four equivalent characterizations
of Koszulity established there. The present theorem extends this
to all genera via the genus induction of clause~(D2).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Non-circularity: twisted-tensor cone as primitive anchor]
\label{rem:bar-cobar-twisted-tensor-anchor}
A reader tracking the proof chain might worry that
Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi} is invoked to verify
clause~(v) of the Koszul-equivalences meta-theorem
(Theorem~\ref{thm:koszul-equivalences-meta}), while
Definition~\ref{def:koszul-chiral-algebra} was initially
phrased in bar-cobar terms; this would create an apparent
circularity. The circularity is only apparent. The canonical
anchor is the twisted-product cone identification
Lemma~\ref{lem:twisted-product-cone-counit}, which computes
$K_\tau^L \simeq \operatorname{Cone}(\varepsilon_\tau)[-1]$ by
a direct chain-level decomposition of $d_\cA + d_\cC + d_\tau^L$
(transport of Loday--Vallette~\cite{LV12} \S2.2.5); this lemma
cites no bar-cobar theorem and no Koszul equivalence. The
implication $(\mathrm{ii}) \Rightarrow (\mathrm{v})$ routes
through this cone identification, not through the present
inversion theorem: the twisting-morphism condition
$d_\tau = m_2 \circ (\mathrm{id} \otimes \tau) \circ \Delta$
forces acyclicity of $K_\tau^L$ via
Lemma~\ref{lem:twisted-product-cone-counit}, and acyclicity of
the cone is equivalent to the counit $\varepsilon_\tau$ being a
quasi-isomorphism. Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi} is
therefore a \emph{consequence} of the twisted-tensor anchor, not
an input to the definition it appears to verify.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Higher-genus conditionality on MK3]
\label{rem:higher-genus-mk3-conditionality}
At genus~$0$, Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi} is
unconditional: it follows from genus-$0$ Koszulity
(axiom~\ref{MK:koszul}) alone, via the fundamental theorem of
chiral twisting morphisms
(Theorem~\ref{thm:fundamental-twisting-morphisms}).
At genus~$g \geq 1$, the proof of clause~(2) invokes
axiom~\ref{MK:modular} (modular Koszulity: PBW degeneration at
genus~$g$, equivalently diagonal Ext vanishing;
Definition~\ref{def:modular-koszul-chiral}), which is verified
for Heisenberg, affine Kac--Moody at non-critical level, Virasoro,
and principal $\cW$-algebras
(Theorems~\ref{thm:pbw-allgenera-km}--\ref{thm:pbw-allgenera-principal-w}).
For an arbitrary Koszul chiral algebra not on this list,
higher-genus inversion is \emph{conditional} on~\ref{MK:modular}.
The genus-$0$ statement and the spectral-sequence collapse
(clause~(4)) remain unconditional.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Homotopy level of bar-cobar inversion]
\label{rem:bar-cobar-inversion-linfty}
The quasi-isomorphism $\Omega(\barB(\cA)) \xrightarrow{\sim} \cA$
lifts to an $L_\infty$-quasi-isomorphism at the homotopy level, by
functoriality of bar-cobar through the $L_\infty$-convolution
$\Convinf$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:operadic-homotopy-convolution}).
In particular, bar-cobar inversion preserves the full quantum
$L_\infty$ structure, not merely the dg~Lie shadow.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Quasi-isomorphism of chain complexes vs chiral algebras]\label{rem:qi-vs-homology-iso}
The distinction is between two levels of structure:

\emph{Chain complex quasi-isomorphism.} A chain map $\psi: C^\bullet \to D^\bullet$ inducing an isomorphism $H^\bullet(\psi): H^\bullet(C) \xrightarrow{\cong} H^\bullet(D)$ on cohomology. This is the standard notion; a ``homology isomorphism'' and a ``quasi-isomorphism'' are the \emph{same thing} at the chain complex level.

\emph{Chiral algebra quasi-isomorphism.} An $A_\infty$ (or chiral algebra) morphism $\psi\colon \mathcal{A} \to \mathcal{B}$ whose linear component $\psi_1\colon \mathcal{A} \to \mathcal{B}$ is a chain complex quasi-isomorphism. Such a map preserves the full $A_\infty$ structure up to coherent homotopy. The distinction matters:
A chain complex quasi-isomorphism tells us only about $H^\bullet$ and need not respect multiplicative or $A_\infty$ structure, whereas a chiral algebra quasi-isomorphism gives a full equivalence in the derived category of chiral algebras, preserving all homotopy-theoretic information. For bar-cobar inversion to establish derived equivalences, the map $\Omega(B(\mathcal{A})) \to \mathcal{A}$ must be a quasi-isomorphism of \emph{chiral algebras}, not of chain complexes alone.

\emph{Example.}
Consider a dga $(C^\bullet, d, \mu)$ with:
\[\cdots \to 0 \to \mathbb{C} \xrightarrow{0} \mathbb{C} \to 0 \to \cdots\]

This has $H^0 = \mathbb{C}$, $H^i = 0$ for $i \neq 0$.

Compare with the algebra $(D^\bullet, 0, \nu) = (\mathbb{C}, 0, 0)$ in degree 0.
The projection $\pi: C^\bullet \to D^\bullet$ is a quasi-isomorphism of chain
complexes (both have $H^0 = \mathbb{C}$), but $\pi$ does \emph{not} respect the
multiplication ($\pi$ need not intertwine $\mu$ and $\nu$ at the chain level).
To obtain a quasi-isomorphism of \emph{algebras}, one must work with $A_\infty$
morphisms, which encode the higher homotopies relating the two multiplicative
structures.
\end{remark}


\begin{remark}[Derived Morita equivalence and the Koszul conductor]
\label{rem:bar-morita-koszul-conductor}
\ClaimStatusConjectured
\index{derived Morita equivalence!bar coalgebra characterization}
\index{Koszul conductor!Morita obstruction}
Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi} converts the bar coalgebra
into a complete derived invariant: two Koszul chiral algebras
$\cA$, $\cB$ are derived Morita equivalent (quasi-isomorphic as
objects of the bar-cobar localization) if and only if their bar
coalgebras $\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)$ and
$\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cB)$ are quasi-isomorphic as dg~coalgebras.
The Koszul conductor $K(\cA) = \kappa(\cA) + \kappa(\cA^!)$
(\S\ref{sec:complementarity}) controls the rigidity of this
identification.

When $K = 0$ (affine Kac--Moody at non-critical level, Heisenberg,
free fields), the complementarity $\kappa(\cA^!) = -\kappa(\cA)$
permits non-trivial bar-coalgebra identifications
$\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA) \simeq \bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cB)$
with $\cA \not\simeq \cB$ as chiral algebras; level-rank duality
provides the prototype.
When $K \neq 0$ (Virasoro with $K = 13$, Bershadsky--Polyakov with
$K = 196$), a quasi-isomorphism of bar coalgebras forces
$\kappa(\cA) = \kappa(\cB)$ and $\kappa(\cA^!) = \kappa(\cB^!)$
simultaneously, since $K$ is an invariant of the bar coalgebra.
The non-vanishing conductor therefore provides a numerical
obstruction to derived Morita equivalence that has no counterpart
in the $K = 0$ families.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Proof strategy and filtration}

\begin{definition}[Bar-cobar filtration]\label{def:bar-cobar-filtration}
Define a decreasing filtration on $\Omega(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A}))$ by:
\[F^p\Omega(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A})) = \bigoplus_{n \geq p} \Omega^n(\bar{B}^n(\mathcal{A}))\]

This is the filtration by \emph{bar degree} (= cobar degree).

\emph{Geometric meaning.} $F^p$ consists of elements involving at least $p$ points
in configuration space. As $p \to \infty$, we are considering increasingly complicated
configurations.

\emph{Properties.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item $F^0 \supseteq F^1 \supseteq F^2 \supseteq \cdots$
\item $\bigcap_{p=0}^\infty F^p = 0$ (completeness)
\item The differential respects filtration: $d(F^p) \subseteq F^p$
\item The natural map factors through the filtration
\end{enumerate}
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Associated graded; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{lem:bar-cobar-associated-graded}
The associated graded of the bar-cobar filtration is:
\[\text{Gr}^p\Omega(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A})) = \Omega^p(\bar{B}^p(\mathcal{A}))\]

The induced differential on $\text{Gr}^\bullet$ is the \emph{bar complex differential} $d_{\bar{B}} = d_{\text{internal}} + d_{\text{bar}}$ (i.e., the full differential on $\bar{B}(\mathcal{A})$, lifted to each cobar tensor factor).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
By definition of associated graded:
\[\text{Gr}^p = F^p / F^{p+1} = \Omega^p(\bar{B}^p(\mathcal{A}))\]

The full differential on $\Omega(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A}))$ decomposes as $d = d_{\bar{B}} + d_{\text{cobar}}$, where $d_{\bar{B}} = d_{\text{internal}} + d_{\text{bar}}$ is the lift of the bar complex differential to each cobar tensor factor (preserving cobar degree~$p$), and $d_{\text{cobar}}$ is the comultiplication-induced part (raising cobar degree by~$1$). On the associated graded $\text{Gr}^p = F^p/F^{p+1}$, only the \emph{filtration-preserving} component survives: $d_{\text{cobar}}$ maps $F^p$ into $F^{p+1}$ and so vanishes on $\text{Gr}^p$. Thus $d_{\text{gr}} = d_{\bar{B}}$, which is the $d_0$ differential of the spectral sequence (cf.\ Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-spectral-sequence}).
\end{proof}

\subsection{Spectral sequence construction}

\begin{theorem}[Bar-cobar spectral sequence; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:bar-cobar-spectral-sequence}
\label{thm:koszul-spectral-sequence}
\textup{[Regime: square-zero total differential on the filtered
bar-cobar complex.]}
Assume the total differential on $\Omega(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A}))$
satisfies $d^2 = 0$ and preserves the filtration from
Definition~\ref{def:bar-cobar-filtration}. Then the filtration from
Definition~\ref{def:bar-cobar-filtration} induces a spectral
sequence:
\[E_0^{p,q} = \left(F^p / F^{p+1}\right)^{p+q} \implies H^{p+q}(\Omega(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A})))\]
converging to the cohomology of $\Omega(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A}))$. Here $p$ is the filtration degree (cobar degree) and $q$ is the complementary degree (from the internal and bar gradings), so the total degree is $p + q$.

\emph{Explicit description of pages.}
\begin{align*}
E_0^{p,q} &= \left(F^p\Omega^{p+q}(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A})) \big/ F^{p+1}\Omega^{p+q}(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A}))\right) \quad \text{(associated graded)} \\
E_1^{p,q} &= H^{p+q}\!\left(E_0^{p,\bullet},\, d_{\bar{B}}\right)
 \quad \text{(bar cohomology at fixed cobar degree $p$)} \\
E_2^{p,q} &= H^p\!\left(E_1^{\bullet,q},\, d_{\text{cobar}}\right)
 \quad \text{(cohomology w.r.t.\ comultiplication-induced differential)} \\
E_\infty^{p,q} &= \mathrm{Gr}^p H^{p+q}(\Omega(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A}))) \quad \text{(limiting page)}
\end{align*}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
This is a standard spectral sequence associated to a filtered complex (Weibel~\cite{Weibel94}, Chapter~5). We verify the key properties:

\emph{Step 1: $E_0$ page.} This is just the raw complex with its bigrading:
\[E_0^{p,q} = F^p\Omega^{p+q}(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A})) / F^{p+1}\Omega^{p+q}(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A}))\]

By definition of the filtration, this isolates the piece in cobar degree~$p$ and total degree $p+q$.

\emph{Step 2: $d_0$ differential.} On the $E_0$ page:
\[d_0: E_0^{p,q} \to E_0^{p,q+1}\]
is the bar complex differential $d_{\bar{B}} = d_{\text{internal}} + d_{\text{bar}}$, lifted to each cobar tensor factor. This is the filtration-preserving component of $d$: both $d_{\text{internal}}$ (from the differential on~$\mathcal{A}$) and $d_{\text{bar}}$ (from the multiplication of~$\mathcal{A}$, encoding collisions) preserve cobar degree.

Taking cohomology gives the $E_1$ page: bar cohomology at each fixed cobar degree.

\emph{Step 3: $d_1$ differential.} On the $E_1$ page:
\[d_1: E_1^{p,q} \to E_1^{p+1,q}\]
is induced by $d_{\text{cobar}}$ (the comultiplication on $\bar{B}(\mathcal{A})$, which increases cobar degree by~$1$).

Taking cohomology gives the $E_2$ page.

\emph{Step 4: Higher differentials.} For $r \geq 2$:
\[d_r: E_r^{p,q} \to E_r^{p+r,q-r+1}\]

These differentials encode higher-order interactions between bar and cobar operations.

\emph{Step 5: Convergence.} The spectral sequence converges because:
For the application to Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi}, the completeness statement in Definition~\ref{def:bar-cobar-filtration}(2) is supplied by its conilpotency/completion hypothesis: if $\bar{B}(\mathcal{A})$ is conilpotent in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:conilpotent-complete}, every element has finite bar degree, while in the augmentation-ideal completion regime the filtration is complete by construction.
\begin{enumerate}
\item The filtration is complete: $\bigcap_p F^p = 0$
\item The filtration is exhaustive: $\bigcup_p F^p = \Omega(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A}))$
\item The complex is bounded in each column (fixed $p$)
\end{enumerate}

By standard spectral sequence theory (Weibel \cite{Weibel94}, Chapter 5), this ensures:
\[E_\infty^{p,q} = \text{Gr}^p H^{p+q}(\Omega(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A})))\]
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Collapse at \texorpdfstring{$E_2$}{E2}; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:spectral-sequence-collapse}
\textup{[Regime: quadratic, Koszul locus, square-zero total differential
\textup{(}Convention~\textup{\ref{conv:regime-tags})}.]}

For the Heisenberg algebra, the spectral sequence collapsed trivially because $d_{\mathrm{bracket}} = 0$ (no simple poles): the bar cohomology was concentrated in degrees $0$ and $2$ without further work (\S\ref{sec:frame-bar-all}). For non-abelian algebras, the collapse is a consequence of the Koszul property.

For a Koszul chiral algebra $\mathcal{A}$ (Remark~\ref{rem:koszul-chiral}) on the
strict square-zero surface of Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-spectral-sequence}, the spectral sequence from
Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-spectral-sequence} collapses at the $E_2$ page:
\[E_2^{p,q} = E_\infty^{p,q}.\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The Koszul property of $\mathcal{A}$ means that the natural inclusion $\iota: \mathcal{A}^! \hookrightarrow \bar{B}(\mathcal{A})$ of the quadratic dual into the bar complex is a quasi-isomorphism (see \cite[Theorem~3.4.1]{LV12} for the classical case and Chapter~\ref{chap:koszul-pairs} for the chiral adaptation). Since $\mathcal{A}^!$ is generated in weight~1 with quadratic relations, its image under $\iota$ lies on the diagonal $p + q = \text{const}$ in the bigrading $(p,q)$ by bar degree and internal degree.

At the $E_1$ page, we compute the cohomology of each column with respect to $d_0 = d_{\bar{B}}$, the full bar complex differential. Each column $E_0^{p,\bullet}$ with differential $d_0$ computes the bar cohomology $H^q(\bar{B}^p(\mathcal{A}), d_{\bar{B}})$ at fixed cobar degree~$p$. By the Koszul quasi-isomorphism, the bar cohomology is concentrated on the diagonal, giving $E_1^{p,q} = 0$ whenever $q \neq 0$ (after reindexing by the bar filtration degree).

At the $E_2$ page, we take cohomology with respect to $d_1$ (induced by $d_{\text{cobar}}$, the comultiplication part). The $E_2$ groups inherit the diagonal concentration.

For $r \geq 2$, the differential $d_r: E_r^{p,q} \to E_r^{p+r, q-r+1}$ shifts the bidegree by $(r, 1-r)$. Since $E_2^{p,q} = 0$ for $q \neq 0$, either the source or the target of $d_r$ vanishes for every $r \geq 2$. Therefore $d_r = 0$ for all $r \geq 2$, and the spectral sequence collapses at $E_2$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Square-zero boundary of the spectral-sequence proof]
\label{rem:spectral-sequence-square-zero-boundary}
Theorems~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-spectral-sequence}
and~\ref{thm:spectral-sequence-collapse} are statements about filtered
complexes with square-zero total differential. In this chapter they
apply to the strict genus-$0$ bar-cobar complex, and to any
completed/corrected model whose total differential squares to zero.
They do \emph{not} apply to the curved fiberwise higher-genus
differential $\dfib$ with
$\dfib^{\,2} = \kappa(\cA)\cdot\omega_g$. Off the Koszul locus, the
proved replacement is the coderived bar-degree filtration of
Proposition~\ref{prop:coderived-bar-degree-spectral-sequence},
together with the intrinsic coderived/contraderived bar-coalgebra
comparison of Theorem~\ref{thm:positselski-chiral-proved}. Ordinary
derived reduction remains available only on the flat finite-type
completed-dual loci of Theorem~\ref{thm:full-derived-module-equiv-proved}
or when the curvature collapses.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Convergence at all genera}

\begin{theorem}[Genus-graded convergence; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:genus-graded-convergence}
\textup{[Regime: curved-central on the Koszul locus
\textup{(}Convention~\textup{\ref{conv:regime-tags})}.]}

Let $\mathcal{A}$ be a Koszul chiral algebra satisfying the strict
Koszul-lane hypotheses of
Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi}. The bar-cobar inversion
$\psi: \Omega(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A})) \to \mathcal{A}$
converges at each genus $g$, and the full genus-graded sum converges in the
$\hbar$-adic completion.

More precisely:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Genus zero:} 
 \[\psi_0: \Omega_0(\bar{B}_0(\mathcal{A})) \xrightarrow{\sim} \mathcal{A}\]
 is a quasi-isomorphism (classical result, BD §3.7)
 
\item \emph{Fixed genus $g$:}
 \[\psi_g: \Omega_g(\bar{B}_g(\mathcal{A})) \to \mathcal{A}_g\]
 is a quasi-isomorphism after appropriate quantum corrections (here $\mathcal{A}_g$ denotes the genus-$g$ component of the genus-graded chiral algebra)
 
\item \emph{Genus series:}
 \[\psi = \sum_{g=0}^\infty \hbar^{2g-2} \psi_g\]
 converges in the $\hbar$-adic completion for $|\hbar| < R$ (radius determined 
 by growth of moduli spaces)
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
We prove each case separately.

\emph{Case 1: Genus zero on~$\bP^1$.}

At genus zero, the chiral bar complex lives on configuration spaces of the rational curve:
\[\bar{B}_0^n(\mathcal{A}) = \Gamma\left(\overline{C}_n(\mathbb{P}^1),
\mathcal{A}^{\boxtimes n} \otimes \Omega^\bullet\right)\]
This is \emph{not} the classical bar complex over a point: the Fulton--MacPherson compactifications $\overline{C}_n(\bP^1)$, the logarithmic propagator $\eta_{ij} = d\log(z_i - z_j)$, and the Arnold relations in the cohomology of configuration spaces are all genuinely present and have no classical analogue. The classical bar over a point embeds via formal-disk restriction followed by homotopy transfer, but this comparison requires specifying the retraction $\bA^1 \to \mathrm{pt}$ and its attendant chain homotopy (see the discussion following Definition~\ref{def:chiral-koszul-pair}).

Beilinson--Drinfeld proved \cite{BD04} Theorem 3.7.11:
\[\Omega_0(\bar{B}_0(\mathcal{A})) \xrightarrow{\sim} \mathcal{A}\]

Their proof uses the Chevalley--Cousin resolution, the Ran space formalism on~$\bP^1$, and descent from the FM compactifications of configuration spaces; it is inherently a statement about the curve~$\bP^1$, not about a point.

We have verified (Theorem~\ref{thm:BD-extension-higher-genus}) that all technical
conditions hold at genus zero.

\emph{Case 2: Fixed genus $g \geq 1$.}

The genus-$g$ quasi-isomorphism $\psi_g$ is proved as
Theorem~\ref{thm:higher-genus-inversion} by induction on~$g$.
The proof proceeds in three steps, none of which invoke
bar-cobar inversion at genus~$g$ as input:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Open stratum.}
On the locus $U_g \subset \overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$ of smooth
curves, the fiberwise bar-cobar counit on each fixed
curve~$X_s$ is a quasi-isomorphism by
axiom~\ref{MK:modular}
(PBW concentration at genus~$g$, verified independently by
Theorems~\ref{thm:pbw-allgenera-km}--\ref{thm:pbw-allgenera-principal-w})
and the fundamental theorem of chiral twisting morphisms
(Theorem~\ref{thm:fundamental-twisting-morphisms}).
See Lemma~\ref{lem:higher-genus-open-stratum-qi}.

\item \emph{Boundary strata.}
Each boundary stratum $D_\Gamma \subset
\partial\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$ decomposes via nodal
gluing into lower-genus pieces. The induction hypothesis
gives a quasi-isomorphism on each vertex, and
K\"unneth at nodes assembles the global statement
(Lemma~\ref{lem:higher-genus-boundary-qi}).

\item \emph{Extension.}
The open-stratum and boundary quasi-isomorphisms together
cover the normal-crossing stratification of
$\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$. A Mayer--Vietoris argument
extends to a global quasi-isomorphism
(Lemma~\ref{lem:extension-across-boundary-qi}).
\end{enumerate}
The logical chain is non-circular: the antecedent
hypotheses~\ref{MK:koszul}--\ref{MK:modular} of
Definition~\ref{def:modular-koszul-chiral} are verified
independently of bar-cobar inversion, and
Theorem~\ref{thm:higher-genus-inversion} derives inversion
as a consequence.

\begin{lemma}[Proper pushforward preserves quasi-isomorphisms]
\label{lem:pushforward-preserves-qi}
\ClaimStatusProvedElsewhere{}
Let $f \colon Y \to S$ be a proper morphism of finite type
and $\phi \colon \mathcal{F} \to \mathcal{G}$ a quasi-isomorphism
of bounded-below complexes of coherent sheaves on~$Y$.
Then $Rf_*(\phi) \colon Rf_*\mathcal{F}
\xrightarrow{\;\sim\;} Rf_*\mathcal{G}$ is a quasi-isomorphism.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
This is proper base change for the derived pushforward
(see e.g.\ \cite[Proposition~3.4.4]{HTT}).
\end{proof}

\emph{Case 3: Genus series convergence.}

Consider the formal series:
\[\psi(\hbar) = \sum_{g=0}^\infty \hbar^{2g-2} \psi_g\]

\emph{Growth estimate.} By Mirzakhani's results \cite{Mirzakhani}, Weil--Petersson volumes satisfy
\[\mathrm{Vol}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g) \sim (2g)!\]
with factorial growth. Consequently the formal genus series has zero radius of analytic convergence, consistent with the non-Borel-summability of the perturbative string expansion.

\emph{$\hbar$-adic completion.} For rigorous formal computations, work in:
\[\widehat{\Omega}(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A}))_\hbar = \varprojlim_n 
\Omega(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A})) / \hbar^n\]

In this completion, the series converges unconditionally.
\end{proof}

\subsection{The counit of the adjunction}

\begin{proposition}[Counit is quasi-isomorphism; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{prop:counit-qi}
The counit of the bar-cobar adjunction:
\[\epsilon: \bar{B}(\Omega(\mathcal{C})) \longrightarrow \mathcal{C}\]
for a chiral coalgebra $\mathcal{C}$ is also a quasi-isomorphism (dual statement).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Verdier duality (Theorem~\ref{thm:verdier-bar-cobar}), the counit $\epsilon_{\mathcal{C}} \colon \bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\Omega^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal{C})) \to \mathcal{C}$ is the Verdier dual of the unit $\eta_{\mathcal{A}^!}$, which is a quasi-isomorphism by Theorem~\ref{thm:geom-unit}. Since Verdier duality on the Fulton--MacPherson compactifications preserves quasi-isomorphisms (Theorem~\ref{thm:verdier-bar-cobar}), the result follows.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Functoriality of the quasi-isomorphism}

\begin{theorem}[Functoriality of bar-cobar inversion; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-functorial}
% NOTE: removed duplicate label thm:cobar-functorial which conflated
% functoriality of the inversion qi with functoriality of the cobar functor.
The quasi-isomorphism $\psi: \Omega(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A})) \xrightarrow{\sim} \mathcal{A}$ 
is \emph{functorial}: for any morphism $f: \mathcal{A} \to \mathcal{A}'$ of 
chiral algebras, the diagram commutes:

\begin{center}
\begin{tikzcd}
\Omega(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A})) \ar[r, "\psi"] \ar[d, "\Omega(\bar{B}(f))"] 
& \mathcal{A} \ar[d, "f"] \\
\Omega(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A}')) \ar[r, "\psi'"] 
& \mathcal{A}'
\end{tikzcd}
\end{center}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
This follows from the functoriality of the bar construction (Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-functorial}) and the universal property of the bar-cobar adjunction (Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-adjunction}).

\emph{Step 1:} The bar construction is functorial:
\[\bar{B}(f): \bar{B}(\mathcal{A}) \to \bar{B}(\mathcal{A}')\]

\emph{Step 2:} The cobar construction is functorial:
\[\Omega(g): \Omega(\mathcal{C}) \to \Omega(\mathcal{C}')\]
for any coalgebra morphism $g$.

\emph{Step 3:} The natural transformation $\psi$ is defined universally via the 
adjunction, hence commutes with all morphisms.

\emph{Step 4:} At each genus, $\psi_g$ is natural in $\mathcal{A}$, so the 
genus-graded sum is also natural.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Applications to module categories}

\begin{remark}[Ordinary module Koszul duality is a separate genus-$0$ surface]
\label{rem:derived-equiv-scope}
The intrinsic higher-genus comparison proved in this chapter is the
bar-coalgebra statement of
Theorems~\ref{thm:positselski-chiral-proved} and
\ref{thm:full-derived-module-equiv-proved}: coderived/contraderived on
the bar-coalgebra surface, with ordinary derived reduction only on the
flat finite-type completed-dual loci. That does \emph{not} by itself
prove a broad ordinary-derived equivalence between general chiral
$\cA$-modules and $\cA^!$-comodules.

The ordinary module-theoretic Koszul duality used elsewhere in the
manuscript is the separate $\Eone$ complete/conilpotent theorem
Theorem~\ref{thm:e1-module-koszul-duality} on the quadratic genus-$0$
bar-dual lane. Outside that lane, one must keep the intrinsic
bar-coalgebra comparison, and any additional module-category rewrite
requires extra hypotheses not supplied by the present chapter.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Physical significance]\label{rem:qi-matters-physics}
From the physics perspective, the distinction between homology isomorphism and 
quasi-isomorphism corresponds to:

A homology isomorphism gives only on-shell equivalence: physical states match, but scattering amplitudes and quantum corrections are inaccessible. A quasi-isomorphism gives off-shell equivalence: correlation functions, amplitudes, quantum corrections (encoded in the higher homotopies), and the path integral measure all transfer.
\end{remark}

%================================================================
% COMPLETED BAR-COBAR INVERSION
%================================================================

\subsection{Completed bar-cobar inversion}
\label{subsec:completed-bar-cobar-inversion}

The finite-stage inversion theorem
(Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi}) establishes the
quasi-isomorphism $\Omega(\barB(\cA)) \xrightarrow{\sim} \cA$ on the
Koszul locus of finite-type chiral algebras. The programmatic regime
($\mathcal{W}_\infty$, affine Yangians, RTT towers) requires an
extension of inversion to separated complete inverse limits. The key
structural input is the strong completion-tower framework developed in
\S\ref{sec:curved-koszul-i-adic}
(Definition~\ref{def:strong-completion-tower},
Theorem~\ref{thm:completed-bar-cobar-strong}); what follows gives the
homological comparison lemma that underlies the inverse-limit passage
and develops the inversion-side consequences of the completion closure
$\CompCl(\Fft)$ (Definition~\ref{def:completion-closure}).

\begin{lemma}[Complete filtered comparison lemma; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{lem:complete-filtered-comparison}
\index{complete filtered comparison lemma|textbf}
\index{Mittag--Leffler!complete filtered comparison}
Let $f\colon C \to D$ be a morphism of separated complete filtered
cochain complexes, with descending filtrations
$F^\bullet C$ and $F^\bullet D$ satisfying:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item the quotient towers are surjective: for every~$N$, the
 transition maps $C/F^{N+2}C \twoheadrightarrow C/F^{N+1}C$ and
 $D/F^{N+2}D \twoheadrightarrow D/F^{N+1}D$ are surjections;
\item every quotient map is a quasi-isomorphism:
 \[
 f_N \colon C/F^{N+1}C \xrightarrow{\;\sim\;} D/F^{N+1}D
 \]
 for all~$N \ge 0$.
\end{enumerate}
Then $f$ is a quasi-isomorphism.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Consider the mapping cone $\operatorname{Cone}(f)$, which inherits a
separated complete filtration from~$C$ and~$D$. Each quotient
$\operatorname{Cone}(f)/F^{N+1} \cong \operatorname{Cone}(f_N)$ is
acyclic because $f_N$ is a quasi-isomorphism by hypothesis~(ii).
The Milnor exact sequence for the inverse system
$\{\operatorname{Cone}(f_N)\}_{N \ge 0}$ reads
\[
0 \to \varprojlim\nolimits^1_N
 H^{m-1}(\operatorname{Cone}(f_N))
\to H^m(\operatorname{Cone}(f))
\to \varprojlim_N H^m(\operatorname{Cone}(f_N)) \to 0.
\]
The right-hand term vanishes because every
$H^m(\operatorname{Cone}(f_N)) = 0$. For the left-hand term: the
quotient tower is surjective by hypothesis~(i), so the transition maps
on each cohomology group form a surjective inverse system of zero
groups, and the Mittag--Leffler condition is satisfied trivially.
Hence $\varprojlim^1 = 0$. It follows that
$H^m(\operatorname{Cone}(f)) = 0$ for all~$m$, so $f$ is a
quasi-isomorphism.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Role in the completed bar-cobar theorem]
\label{rem:complete-filtered-comparison-role}
Lemma~\ref{lem:complete-filtered-comparison} is the homological
workhorse of the completed bar-cobar theorem
(Theorem~\ref{thm:completed-bar-cobar-strong}). In that application,
$C = \widehat\Omega^{\mathrm{ch}}(\widehat{\bar B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA))$,
$D = \cA$, and the quotient quasi-isomorphisms $f_N$ are the
finite-stage counits
$\epsilon_N\colon \Omega^{\mathrm{ch}}(\bar B^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA_{\le N}))
\xrightarrow{\sim} \cA_{\le N}$, which are quasi-isomorphisms by the
finite-type regime. The surjectivity of the quotient tower follows from
the strong completion-tower axiom: the projections
$\cA_{\le N+1} \twoheadrightarrow \cA_{\le N}$ are strict surjections
by construction. The lemma then gives the completed counit
$\widehat\epsilon$ is a quasi-isomorphism; this is Step~3 of the proof of
Theorem~\ref{thm:completed-bar-cobar-strong}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Completed inversion: the inversion-side summary]
\label{rem:completed-inversion-summary}
The completion closure theory
(Definition~\ref{def:completion-closure}--Theorem~\ref{thm:uniform-pbw-bridge},
developed in \S\ref{sec:curved-koszul-i-adic}) gives a complete
inversion package for the programmatic regime:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Domain.}
 $\CompCl(\Fft)$ is the class of strong completion towers
 (Definition~\ref{def:strong-completion-tower}) with finite-type
 quotients.
\item \emph{Inversion.}
 Completed bar and cobar are quasi-inverse on $\CompCl(\Fft)$
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:completed-bar-cobar-strong}).
\item \emph{Homotopy category.}
 Localizing by quotientwise quasi-isomorphisms gives an equivalence
 of homotopy categories
 (Corollary~\ref{cor:completion-closure-equivalence}).
\item \emph{Stability under twisting.}
 If $\alpha \in F^1\cA^1$ is a continuous Maurer--Cartan element,
 then $\cA_\alpha \in \CompCl(\Fft)$ and inversion persists
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:mc-twisting-closure}).
\item \emph{Representability.}
 Algebra and coalgebra maps between completed objects are represented
 by continuous twisting morphisms
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:completed-twisting-representability}).
\item \emph{Verification criteria.}
 Coefficient stability
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:coefficient-stability-criterion}) reduces
 completed inversion to stabilization of finite matrix entries on
 windows; the uniform PBW bridge
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:uniform-pbw-bridge}) connects PBW concentration
 (MC1) directly to completed duality (MC4).
\end{enumerate}
Together with the finite-stage inversion theorem
(Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi}), these results close
Ring~1 of the monograph across all four regimes: quadratic,
curved-central, filtered-complete, and programmatic.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[Completed derived equivalence; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:completed-derived-equivalence}
\index{derived equivalence!completed}
Let $\cA \in \CompCl(\Fft)$ be a strong completion tower on a
smooth curve~$X$. Then the completed bar and cobar functors induce
an equivalence of triangulated categories
\[
\mathcal{D}^b(\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{cts}}(\cA))
\;\simeq\;
\mathcal{D}^b(\operatorname{Comod}^{\mathrm{pronil}}
(\widehat{\bar B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA))),
\]
where $\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{cts}}$ denotes continuous modules
over the complete algebra and
$\operatorname{Comod}^{\mathrm{pronil}}$ denotes pronilpotent
comodules over the completed bar coalgebra. The twisting morphism
$\widehat\tau\colon \widehat{\bar B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA) \to \cA$
mediates the equivalence via completed extension of scalars.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The completed counit and unit are quasi-isomorphisms by
Theorem~\ref{thm:completed-bar-cobar-strong}(3)--(4). The
passage to module/comodule categories follows from completed twisting
representability
(Theorem~\ref{thm:completed-twisting-representability}), which
ensures that the completed bar and cobar functors on
module categories are adjoint and that the unit/counit natural
transformations are quasi-isomorphisms quotientwise. Applying
Lemma~\ref{lem:complete-filtered-comparison} to each module/comodule
then gives the equivalence. The argument parallels
Theorem~\ref{thm:full-derived-module-equiv-proved}, with
finite-generation replaced by continuity and conilpotence replaced
by pronilpotence.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[From finite-type to programmatic: the four-regime inversion table]
\label{rem:four-regime-inversion}
\index{bar-cobar inversion!four-regime table}
The following table summarizes the inversion theorem across all four
regimes (Convention~\ref{conv:regime-tags}):
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{@{}llll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Regime} & \textbf{Input} & \textbf{Category}
 & \textbf{Inversion} \\
\midrule
Quadratic &
 Koszulness &
 $D^b(\mathrm{Mod}^{\mathrm{fg}})$ &
 Thm~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi} \\
Curved-central &
 + $I$-adic completion &
 coderived &
 Cor~\ref{cor:bar-cobar-inverse} \\
Filtered-complete &
 + pronilpotent filtration &
 contraderived &
 \S\ref{subsec:positselski-chiral-equivalence} \\
Programmatic &
 strong completion tower &
 $D^b(\mathrm{Mod}^{\mathrm{cts}})$ &
 Thm~\ref{thm:completed-bar-cobar-strong} \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The first three rows are available at finite type; the fourth extends
to infinite-generator algebras via the completion closure
$\CompCl(\Fft)$. The passage from row~$1$ to row~$4$ is
mediated by the degree cutoff (Lemma~\ref{lem:degree-cutoff}), which
makes the infinite bar differential into a quotientwise finite sum,
and the complete filtered comparison lemma
(Lemma~\ref{lem:complete-filtered-comparison}), which passes the
quotientwise quasi-isomorphisms to the inverse limit.
\end{remark}

%================================================================
% GEOMETRIC AND CATEGORICAL CHARACTERIZATIONS OF CHIRAL KOSZULNESS
%================================================================

\subsection{Geometric and categorical characterizations of chiral Koszulness}
\label{subsec:geometric-categorical-koszulness}

The inversion theorem (Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi})
identifies chiral Koszulness as the condition under which bar-cobar
inversion is a quasi-isomorphism. We give five characterizations
of this condition (descent, factorization homology, FM boundary
acyclicity, $\mathcal{D}$-module purity, Lagrangian geometry):
three are proved equivalent to Koszulness
(Theorem~\ref{thm:koszul-equivalences-meta}),
one is conditional on perfectness, and one ($\mathcal{D}$-module
purity) remains partially proved (forward direction only).
Their common theme is that Koszulness is a
\emph{finiteness and regularity} condition: the bar complex has
the simplest possible behavior.

\medskip

\subsubsection{Barr--Beck--Lurie characterization}

Lurie's $\infty$-categorical Barr--Beck theorem~\cite[Theorem~4.7.3.5]{HA}
characterizes (co)monadic adjunctions by conservativity and totalization
preservation. We conjecture that $B_\kappa \dashv \Omega_\kappa$%
\footnote{Following Remark~\ref{rem:adjunction-direction-convention},
the canonical direction is $\Omega_\kappa \dashv B_\kappa$
(cobar left adjoint to bar). The notation $B_\kappa \dashv
\Omega_\kappa$ used here lists the right adjoint first; the
mathematical content (unit, counit, Barr--Beck conditions on
$B_\kappa$) is the same.}
satisfies these conditions precisely on the Koszul locus.

\begin{theorem}[Barr--Beck--Lurie characterization of chiral Koszulness;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:barr-beck-lurie-koszulness}
\index{Koszulness!Barr--Beck--Lurie characterization}
\index{bar-cobar adjunction!Barr--Beck--Lurie conditions}
Let $\cA$ be a chiral algebra on a smooth curve~$X$ satisfying the
standing hypotheses of Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi}}.
The bar-cobar adjunction $B_\kappa \dashv \Omega_\kappa$ satisfies the
Barr--Beck--Lurie conditions:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \textup{(Conservativity)}\quad
 $B_\kappa$ detects equivalences: a morphism $f \colon \cA \to \cA'$
 of chiral algebras is a quasi-isomorphism if and only if
 $B_\kappa(f)$ is.
\item \textup{(Totalization preservation)}\quad
 $B_\kappa$ preserves totalizations of $B_\kappa$-split cosimplicial
 objects in the $\infty$-category of chiral algebras.
\item \textup{(Comparison equivalence)}\quad
 $\cA$ is chirally Koszul if and only if the Barr--Beck--Lurie
 comparison functor
 \[
 \Phi \colon \operatorname{Mod}(\cA)
 \longrightarrow \operatorname{Comod}^{B_\kappa}(B(\cA))
 \]
 is an equivalence.
\end{enumerate}
Here the comonad is $G = B_\kappa \circ \Omega_\kappa$, and
$\operatorname{Comod}^{B_\kappa}(B(\cA))$ denotes $G$-coalgebras
in conilpotent comodules over the bar coalgebra. The comparison functor
sends a module~$M$ to the totalization of the cosimplicial bar-cobar
resolution $G^{\bullet+1}(M)$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Conservativity.}
On the Koszul locus, bar-cobar inversion
(Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi}) gives that the counit
$\varepsilon_\cA \colon \Omega_\kappa(B_\kappa(\cA)) \xrightarrow{\sim} \cA$
is a quasi-isomorphism for every Koszul~$\cA$.
Suppose $f\colon \cA \to \cA'$ is a morphism such that
$B_\kappa(f)$ is a quasi-isomorphism. Since $\Omega_\kappa$ is a
functor, $\Omega_\kappa(B_\kappa(f))$ is also a quasi-isomorphism.
The naturality square for the counit gives
$f \circ \varepsilon_\cA
= \varepsilon_{\cA'} \circ \Omega_\kappa(B_\kappa(f))$;
the right-hand side is a composite of two quasi-isomorphisms
($\varepsilon_{\cA'}$ by bar-cobar inversion for~$\cA'$, and
$\Omega_\kappa(B_\kappa(f))$ by the hypothesis on~$f$),
so $f \circ \varepsilon_\cA$ is a quasi-isomorphism.
Since $\varepsilon_\cA$ is a quasi-isomorphism, $f$~is as well.

\emph{Totalization preservation.}
We must verify that $B_\kappa$ preserves the totalization of any
$B_\kappa$-split cosimplicial object $\cA^\bullet$. The bar complex
is computed fiberwise on configuration spaces:
$B_\kappa(\cA)_n = \Gamma(\overline{\mathrm{Conf}}_n(X),
\mathcal{F}_n)$. On each fiber over a stratum of
$\overline{\mathrm{Conf}}_n(X)$, the bar construction is a
finite-dimensional chain complex: by hypothesis, each conformal
weight space of~$\cA$ is finite-dimensional, and at each degree~$n$
the bar differential preserves the conformal weight grading,
so $\mathcal{F}_n$ is a bounded complex of finite-dimensional
fibers. For a $B_\kappa$-split cosimplicial diagram,
the splittings restrict to each fiber, and the resulting
inverse system of partial totalizations consists of
finite-dimensional cochain complexes at each conformal weight.
Since finite-dimensional vector spaces satisfy the
Mittag--Leffler condition trivially
(cf.~\cite[Proposition~3.5.7]{Weibel94}), we have
$\varprojlim^1 = 0$ for each weight space, whence
totalization commutes with the passage to global sections.

\emph{Comparison equivalence.}
By \cite[Theorem~4.7.3.5]{HA}, conservativity
and totalization preservation of $B_\kappa$ on the Koszul locus
imply that the comparison functor~$\Phi$ is an equivalence.
Conversely, if $\Phi$ is an equivalence then $B_\kappa$ is
necessarily conservative; the bar spectral sequence must
collapse, giving Koszulness by
Theorem~\ref{thm:pbw-koszulness-criterion}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Three-pillar interaction and effective descent]\label{rem:bbl-content}
The three BBL conditions align with the three-pillar architecture
(\S\ref{sec:concordance-three-pillars}): conservativity~(i) is Pillar~B
(the convolution algebra detects quasi-isomorphisms), totalization
preservation~(ii) is Pillar~C (log FM fibers are contractible), and the
comparison equivalence~(iii) is Pillar~A ($\mathrm{Ch}_\infty$ rectifies
to strict chiral). Chiral Koszulness \emph{is} effective descent
for~$B_\kappa$: on the Koszul locus the cosimplicial bar-cobar
resolution converges and $\Phi$ is an equivalence; off it, passage to
the coderived category is required
(\S\ref{subsec:positselski-chiral-equivalence}).
\end{remark}

\medskip

\subsubsection{Factorization homology concentration}

Since the bar complex \emph{is} factorization homology
(Proposition~\ref{prop:bar-fh}), Koszulness acquires a homological
characterization.

\begin{theorem}[Factorization homology concentration;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:fh-concentration-koszulness}
\index{Koszulness!factorization homology characterization}
\index{factorization homology!concentration and Koszulness}
Let $\cA$ be a chiral algebra on a smooth curve~$X$ satisfying the
standing hypotheses. Then $\cA$ is chirally Koszul if and only if for
every smooth projective curve $\Sigma_g$ of genus~$g \geq 0$:
\[
 H^k\Bigl(\textstyle\int_{\Sigma_g} \cA\Bigr) = 0 \quad
 \text{for all } k \neq 0.
\]
Equivalently, the factorization homology $\int_{\Sigma_g} \cA$ is
concentrated in cohomological degree zero for all genera.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Forward: the bar complex is factorization homology
(Proposition~\ref{prop:bar-fh}); $E_2$-collapse
(Theorem~\ref{thm:pbw-koszulness-criterion}) concentrates
$H^*(\int_{\Sigma_g}\cA)$ in degree~$0$.
Converse: at $g = 0$, concentration of
$\int_{\mathbb{P}^1}\cA \simeq |\barBgeom(\cA)|$
forces the bar spectral sequence to collapse, giving
Koszulness by Theorem~\ref{thm:pbw-koszulness-criterion}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Goodwillie filtration]\label{rem:goodwillie-tower-fh}
The factorization homology $\int_X \cA$ admits a Goodwillie-type filtration
by configuration number:
\[
 \textstyle\int_X \cA \;\simeq\;
 \cA \;\oplus\;
 \Conf_2(X) \otimes_{S_2} (s^{-1}\bar{\cA})^{\otimes 2}
 \;\oplus\;
 \Conf_3(X) \otimes_{S_3} (s^{-1}\bar{\cA})^{\otimes 3}
 \;\oplus\; \cdots
\]
The bar spectral sequence
(Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi}) \emph{is} the spectral
sequence of this filtration. PBW concentration
(Theorem~\ref{thm:pbw-koszulness-criterion}) forces $E_2$-collapse,
giving $H^k(\int_X \cA) = 0$ for $k \neq 0$; non-collapse witnesses
failure of Koszulness.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Poincar\'e/Koszul duality]\label{rem:ayala-francis-poincare-koszul}
Ayala--Francis~\cite{AF15} give $\int_X \cA \simeq \int^X \cA^!$,
the factorization-homology incarnation of Theorem~C. On the Koszul
locus, $Q_g(\cA) = H^0(\int_{\Sigma_g} \cA)$: conformal blocks
\emph{are} the full chiral homology, with no higher corrections.
\end{remark}

\medskip

\subsubsection{Fulton--MacPherson boundary acyclicity}

The bar complex lives on $\overline{\Conf}_n(X)$; restriction to
boundary strata encodes OPE residues. Koszulness should be equivalent
to acyclicity of all such restrictions.

\begin{theorem}[FM boundary acyclicity;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:fm-boundary-acyclicity}
\index{Koszulness!FM boundary acyclicity}
\index{Fulton--MacPherson compactification!boundary acyclicity}
Let $\cA$ be a chiral algebra on~$X$ satisfying the standing hypotheses.
Then $\cA$ is chirally Koszul if and only if for all $n \geq 2$ and every
boundary stratum $S \subset \partial \overline{\Conf}_n(X)$ with inclusion
$i_S \colon S \hookrightarrow \overline{\Conf}_n(X)$:
\[
 H^k\bigl(i_S^!\, \barBch_n(\cA)\bigr) = 0
 \quad \text{for all } k \neq 0.
\]
In words: the restriction of the $n$-th bar component to every boundary
stratum of the Fulton--MacPherson compactification is cohomologically
concentrated in degree zero.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Each boundary stratum $S_T \cong \prod_{v \in V(T)}
\overline{\Conf}_{|v|}(X_v)$ is indexed by a tree~$T$.
The restriction $i_{S_T}^!\,\barBch_n(\cA)$ decomposes as
the tensor product $\bigotimes_{v \in V(T)}
i_v^!\,\barBch_{|v|}(\cA)$,
where each factor is a lower-degree bar component restricted to
$\overline{\Conf}_{|v|}(X_v)$.

Forward: $E_2$-collapse
(Theorem~\ref{thm:pbw-koszulness-criterion}) concentrates each
bar component in degree~$0$; restrictions of degree-$0$ objects
remain in degree~$0$.

Converse: at the deepest stratum $S = D_{\{i,j\}}$
(binary collision), $i_S^!\,\barBch_n$ computes the OPE
residue $a_{(k)}b$ at a single collision. Acyclicity for all
binary strata forces the PBW comparison map to be injective
at every weight, giving $E_2$-collapse.
\end{proof}

\medskip

\subsubsection{D-module purity criterion}

The bar components $\barBch_n(\cA)$ are regular holonomic
$\mathcal{D}$-modules (Lemma~\ref{lem:bar-holonomicity}). The classical
Beilinson--Ginzburg--Soergel purity theorem~\cite{BGS96} lifts to the
chiral setting as follows.

\begin{conjecture}[D-module purity criterion;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]\label{conj:d-module-purity-koszulness}
\index{Koszulness!D-module purity criterion}
\index{D-module!purity and Koszulness}
\index{characteristic variety!alignment with FM stratification}
Let $\cA$ be a chiral algebra on~$X$ satisfying the standing hypotheses.
Then $\cA$ is chirally Koszul if and only if the following two conditions
hold for all $n \geq 1$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \textup{(Purity)}\quad
 Each bar component $\barBch_n(\cA)$, viewed as a mixed Hodge module on
 $\overline{\Conf}_n(X)$, is \emph{pure} of weight~$n$.
\item \textup{(Characteristic variety alignment)}\quad
 The characteristic variety
 $\operatorname{Ch}(\barBch_n(\cA)) \subset T^*\overline{\Conf}_n(X)$
 is contained in the union of conormal bundles to boundary strata:
 \[
 \operatorname{Ch}\bigl(\barBch_n(\cA)\bigr) \;\subset\;
 \bigcup_{S \subset \partial \overline{\Conf}_n(X)}
 T^*_S \overline{\Conf}_n(X).
 \]
\end{enumerate}
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[Content and implications]\label{rem:d-module-purity-content-bci}
Condition~(i) is the chiral analogue of the BGS diagonal purity:
$\operatorname{Ext}^i_A(k,k)$ carries a pure Hodge structure of
weight~$i$ if and only if $A$ is Koszul~\cite{BGS96}.
Condition~(ii) asserts that all OPE singularities are visible on the
FM boundary, with no hidden singularities in the interior of
configuration space. For regular holonomic $\mathcal{D}$-modules, this
forces $\barBch_n(\cA)$ to be a successive extension of rank-one flat
connections along boundary strata.

Together, (i) and (ii) imply FM boundary acyclicity
(Theorem~\ref{thm:fm-boundary-acyclicity}): purity forces the Leray
spectral sequence for $i_S^!\,\barBch_n$ to degenerate at~$E_1$, and
alignment puts the $E_1$ terms in degree zero.
In the representation-theoretic context, alignment translates to the
BGG resolution property: highest-weight modules have finite Verma
filtrations.
\end{remark}

\medskip

\subsubsection{Lagrangian criterion in the shifted-symplectic deformation space}

Ambient complementarity
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:ambient-complementarity},
Theorem~\ref{thm:ambient-complementarity-fmp}) equips the modular
deformation space with a $(-1)$-shifted symplectic structure.
Koszulness should be Lagrangian transversality.

\begin{conjecture}[Conditional Lagrangian characterization of chiral Koszulness;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]%
\label{conj:lagrangian-koszulness}%
\index{Koszulness!Lagrangian characterization}
\index{Lagrangian!transversality and Koszulness}
\index{shifted-symplectic!Lagrangian criterion for Koszulness}
Suppose the ambient complementarity tangent complex $T_{\mathrm{comp}}(\cA)$
carries a $(-1)$-shifted symplectic structure~$\omega$ \textup{(}as in
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:ambient-complementarity-fmp})}, and the
one-sided deformation maps
\[
 i_{\cA} \colon \mathcal{M}_{\cA} \longrightarrow \mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{comp}},
 \qquad
 i_{\cA^!} \colon \mathcal{M}_{\cA^!} \longrightarrow \mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{comp}}
\]
are isotropic embeddings. Then $\cA$ is chirally Koszul if and only if both
$i_{\cA}$ and $i_{\cA^!}$ are \emph{Lagrangian} \textup{(}isotropic of maximal
dimension\textup{)}. Equivalently: the bar-cobar adjunction defines a Lagrangian
correspondence in the $(-1)$-shifted symplectic deformation space.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[Evidence]
Forward: on the Koszul locus, the bar-cobar adjunction gives a
free resolution and the complementarity splitting
$\mathbf{Q}_g(\cA) \oplus \mathbf{Q}_g(\cA^!) \simeq
H^*(\overline{\cM}_g, \cZ_\cA)$ (Theorem~C) identifies $\cM_\cA$
and $\cM_{\cA^!}$ as complementary subspaces. The
shifted-symplectic structure
(Theorem~\ref{thm:ambient-complementarity-fmp}) makes them
isotropic; complementarity gives maximal dimension, hence
Lagrangian.

Converse: transverse Lagrangians in a $(-1)$-shifted symplectic
space have derived intersection of expected dimension~$0$. This
derived intersection is the twisted tensor product
$K_\tau(\cA, \cA^!)$; its acyclicity is Koszulness.
This is a Koszul-locus argument. Off the Koszul locus, the chapter
proves only the intrinsic coderived/contraderived bar-coalgebra
comparison of Theorem~\ref{thm:positselski-chiral-proved}, not an
ordinary twisted-tensor-product or free-resolution statement.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[PTVV interpretation]\label{rem:lagrangian-ptvv}
In the PTVV framework~\cite{PTVV13}, the derived intersection
$\mathcal{M}_\cA \times^h_{\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{comp}}}
\mathcal{M}_{\cA^!}$ computes the twisted tensor product
$K_\tau(\cA, \cA^!)$ on the Koszul surface of
Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi}; its acyclicity
\textup{(}equivalent to Koszulness\textup{)} is
precisely the transversality of the two Lagrangians.
The proved linear shadow is Theorem~C:
$Q_g(\cA) \oplus Q_g(\cA^!) \cong
H^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, \mathcal{Z}(\cA))$.
The off-locus coderived surface is not identified here with an
ordinary twisted tensor product.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Conditional hypotheses and their verification]
\label{rem:lagrangian-conditional}
Conjecture~\ref{conj:lagrangian-koszulness} is conditional on three
sub-hypotheses of the ambient complementarity programme: perfectness of
the deformation complex, non-degeneracy of the shifted-symplectic
pairing, and finiteness of the modular envelope. The tangent-level
Lagrangian structure
(Theorem~\ref{thm:ambient-complementarity-fmp}) is proved
unconditionally at the ambient cyclic-deformation level; the characterization of Koszulness as Lagrangian
transversality then follows from the PTVV derived-intersection
computation (Remark~\ref{rem:lagrangian-ptvv}) once the three
sub-hypotheses are verified. Global Lagrangian at the tangent level and
globally Lagrangian are equivalent when the derived intersection is
discrete.

\emph{Verification for the standard landscape.}
Proposition~\ref{prop:lagrangian-perfectness} verifies
perfectness for the standard landscape at non-critical,
non-degenerate levels. The proof proceeds in four steps:
(1)~finite-dimensionality of the deformation complex at
each weight level (from~(P1));
(2)~chain-level nondegeneracy of the cyclic pairing
(the pairing on $\fg = \Defcyc^{\mathrm{mod}}(\cA)$ is
block-diagonal in the $(g,r)$-decomposition, and each block
is a convolution of nondegenerate pairings on finite-dimensional
spaces (the invariant form~(P2) and the cyclic
trace on the modular cooperad));
(3)~skew-adjointness of the differential with respect to the
pairing (a defining property of invariant pairings on dg~Lie
algebras);
(4)~the induced map $\fg|_n \to (\fg|_n)^\vee[-1]$
is a chain isomorphism (a chain map that is a graded isomorphism
is automatically a quasi-isomorphism), hence the pairing is
perfect.
Once perfectness holds, the PTVV principle gives
$\cM_{\mathrm{comp}}$ its $(-1)$-shifted symplectic structure;
finiteness of the modular envelope is immediate from~(P1).
Corollary~\ref{cor:lagrangian-unconditional} upgrades the
Lagrangian criterion to an unconditional equivalence for the
standard-landscape Koszul cases covered by
Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi}. The filtered-complete
off-locus regime remains on the intrinsic coderived/contraderived
bar-coalgebra surface of
Theorem~\ref{thm:positselski-chiral-proved} and is not part of
that upgrade.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Perfectness for the standard landscape]
\label{prop:lagrangian-perfectness}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
\index{Lagrangian!perfectness verification}
\index{perfectness!cyclic pairing on complementarity datum}
Let $\cA$ satisfy the standing hypotheses and the following:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(P\arabic*)}]
\item\label{item:perf-fingen}
 \textup{(Finite weight spaces)}\quad
 The conformal weight spaces $\cA_n$ are finite-dimensional for
 all~$n$, and $\cA_n = 0$ for $n \ll 0$.
\item\label{item:perf-nondeg}
 \textup{(Nondegenerate invariant form)}\quad
 The invariant bilinear form
 $\langle{-},{-}\rangle \colon \cA \otimes \cA \to \omega_X$
 restricts to a nondegenerate pairing on each weight space~$\cA_n$.
\item\label{item:perf-dual}
 \textup{(Dual regularity)}\quad
 The Koszul dual $\cA^!$ also satisfies
 \textup{(P\ref{item:perf-fingen})} and
 \textup{(P\ref{item:perf-nondeg})}.
\end{enumerate}
Then the cyclic pairing on the ambient complementarity datum
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:ambient-complementarity-datum}(v))}
is perfect in the weight-graded pro-complete sense: at each conformal
weight level~$n$, the induced map
\[
(L_\cA \oplus K_\cA \oplus L_{\cA^!})|_n
\;\longrightarrow\;
(L_\cA \oplus K_\cA \oplus L_{\cA^!})^\vee[-1]\big|_n
\]
is an isomorphism of finite-dimensional vector spaces.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The total complex $L_\cA \oplus K_\cA \oplus L_{\cA^!}$ of the
ambient complementarity datum decomposes the modular cyclic
deformation complex $\fg := \Defcyc^{\mathrm{mod}}(\cA)$
(Definition~\ref{def:modular-cyclic-deformation-complex})
relative to the Koszul duality structure: $L_\cA$ governs
$\cA$-deformations, $L_{\cA^!}$ governs $\cA^!$-deformations,
$K_\cA$ governs the twisting interaction. The cyclic pairing
on $L_\cA \oplus K_\cA \oplus L_{\cA^!}$
(Definition~\ref{def:ambient-complementarity-datum}(v))
is the invariant pairing on~$\fg$ expressed in this
decomposition. We prove perfectness of this pairing
weight-by-weight.

Fix a conformal weight level~$n$.

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{Step~1: finite-dimensionality.}
By~(P\ref{item:perf-fingen}), each $\cA_m$ is finite-dimensional
and vanishes for $m \ll 0$. The complex~$\fg$ decomposes at weight~$n$ as
\[
\fg|_n
\;=\;
\bigoplus_{\substack{g,r \\ 2g-2+r>0}}
\operatorname{CoDer}^{\mathrm{cyc}}\bigl(
\barB^{(g,r)}(\cA)
\bigr)[1]\big|_n,
\]
a finite direct sum (only finitely many stable pairs $(g,r)$
contribute at weight~$n$) of finite-dimensional spaces (each
cyclic coderivation space is finite-dimensional because $\cA_m$ is,
and the bar complex at fixed $(g,r)$ is built from finite tensor
products of the~$\cA_m$). Hence $\dim \fg|_n < \infty$.

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{Step~2: chain-level nondegeneracy.}
The degree~$-1$ cyclic pairing~$\omega$ on~$\fg$
is induced from two inputs:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item the invariant form
 $\langle{-},{-}\rangle_\cA$ on~$\cA$, which is nondegenerate on
 each weight space by~(P\ref{item:perf-nondeg});
\item the cyclic trace $\operatorname{tr}_{(g,r)}$ on each component
 of the modular cooperad $\mathcal{P}^!_{(g,r)}$,
 which is nondegenerate by the cyclic
 modular operad axioms (Serre duality on
 $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,r}$).
\end{enumerate}
At each $(g,r)$, the pairing on
$\operatorname{CoDer}^{\mathrm{cyc}}(\barB^{(g,r)}(\cA))[1]|_n
\cong \operatorname{Hom}(\mathcal{P}^!_{(g,r)},
\operatorname{End}^{\mathrm{cyc}}_\cA)|_n$
is the convolution of~(a) and~(b): explicitly,
$\omega(\alpha, \beta)
= \operatorname{tr}_{(g,r)}\bigl(
\langle \alpha(-), \beta(-) \rangle_\cA\bigr)$.
This is nondegenerate because it is the composite of the
canonical isomorphism
$\operatorname{Hom}(V, W) \cong V^\vee \otimes W$
with the tensor-product pairing, and the tensor product of two
nondegenerate finite-dimensional bilinear forms is nondegenerate.
Because the total pairing on~$\fg|_n$ is the direct sum over
$(g,r)$ of these component pairings (different $(g,r)$-components
are $\omega$-orthogonal by the grading), the total chain-level
pairing is nondegenerate.

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{Step~3: skew-adjointness of the differential.}
The differential $d = d_{\mathrm{int}} + d_{\mathrm{sew}}$
on~$\fg$ is skew-adjoint with respect to~$\omega$:
\[
\omega(d\alpha, \beta)
\;+\; (-1)^{|\alpha|}\,\omega(\alpha, d\beta)
\;=\; 0.
\]
This is the defining property of an invariant pairing on a
dg~Lie algebra and follows from
$\omega([\Theta, \alpha], \beta)
= \omega(\alpha, [\Theta, \beta])$
applied to the Maurer--Cartan element~$\Theta_\cA$ that
twists the differential.

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{Step~4: perfectness.}
The pairing~$\omega$ induces a chain map
$\varphi \colon \fg|_n \to (\fg|_n)^\vee[-1]$
defined by $\varphi(\alpha)(\beta) := \omega(\alpha, \beta)$.
That $\varphi$ is a chain map follows from the
skew-adjointness in Step~3: $\varphi \circ d = d^\vee \circ \varphi$.
By Step~2, $\varphi$ is an isomorphism of graded vector spaces
at each chain degree (nondegenerate finite-dimensional bilinear
form $\Leftrightarrow$ the induced linear map is bijective).
A chain map that is an isomorphism of underlying graded vector
spaces is a chain isomorphism, hence a fortiori a
quasi-isomorphism. Therefore the pairing on~$\fg|_n$ is perfect.

Taking the pro-complete limit over all weight levels:
$\omega$ is perfect at each~$n$, so the pro-complete
pairing on~$\fg = \varprojlim_n \fg/F_n$ is perfect.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Unconditional Lagrangian criterion for the
standard landscape]
\label{cor:lagrangian-unconditional}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
\index{Koszulness!Lagrangian criterion unconditional}
\index{Lagrangian!unconditional equivalence}
Under hypotheses \textup{(P1)--(P3)}, and on the Koszul locus to
which Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi} applies, the Lagrangian criterion
\textup{(}item~\textup{(xi)} of the meta-theorem,
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:koszul-equivalences-meta})} is an
unconditional equivalence: $\cA$ is chirally Koszul if and only if
$\mathcal{M}_\cA$ and $\mathcal{M}_{\cA^!}$ are transverse
Lagrangians in the $(-1)$-shifted symplectic deformation
space~$\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{comp}}$.

In particular, this applies unconditionally to every algebra in the
standard landscape at the non-critical, non-degenerate levels for
which Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi} applies:
Heisenberg at $k \neq 0$, affine Kac--Moody $V_k(\fg)$ at
$k \neq -h^\vee$, Virasoro at generic~$c$, principal
$\mathcal{W}$-algebras at non-critical level, and all free-field
families $bc$, $\beta\gamma$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
We verify the shifted-symplectic hypotheses and then prove the two
implications directly on the Koszul surface covered by
Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi}.

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{(1) Formal moduli problem with $(-1)$-shifted symplectic
structure.}
The dg~Lie algebra $\fg := \Defcyc^{\mathrm{mod}}(\cA)$ is
complete and filtered (by genus). By the Lurie--Pridham
correspondence \cite{LurieDAGX, Pridham17}, $\fg$ integrates
to a formal moduli problem $\cM_{\mathrm{comp}}(\cA)$ with
tangent complex $\fg[1]$.
Proposition~\ref{prop:lagrangian-perfectness} gives perfectness
of the degree~$-1$ invariant pairing on~$\fg$
under~(P1)--(P3).
By the PTVV/Kontsevich--Pridham principle \cite{PTVV13,Pridham17},
a perfect invariant pairing of degree~$-1$ on a dg~Lie algebra
induces a $(-1)$-shifted symplectic structure on the
corresponding formal moduli problem. Hence
$\cM_{\mathrm{comp}}(\cA)$ carries a canonical $(-1)$-shifted
symplectic structure.

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{(2) Isotropy.}
The one-sided deformation maps $i_\cA$, $i_{\cA^!}$ are
isotropic embeddings: this is
Theorem~\ref{thm:ambient-complementarity-tangent}(ii), proved
unconditionally.

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{(3) Equivalence on the Koszul surface.}
\begin{itemize}
\item \emph{Forward} (Koszul $\Rightarrow$ Lagrangian).
 On the Koszul locus, the twisted tensor product
 $K_\tau(\cA, \cA^!)$ is acyclic. The complementarity
 splitting (Theorem~C) gives a direct-sum decomposition
 $T_{\mathrm{comp}} \simeq T_\cA \oplus T_{\cA^!}$:
 the one-sided tangent complexes are complementary subspaces.
 By~(2) they are isotropic; by complementarity they are
 half-dimensional. Isotropic + half-dimensional = Lagrangian.
\item \emph{Converse} (Lagrangian $\Rightarrow$ Koszul).
 Transverse Lagrangians in a $(-1)$-shifted symplectic
 formal moduli problem have discrete derived
 intersection~\cite{PTVV13}. The derived intersection
 $\cM_\cA \times^h_{\cM_{\mathrm{comp}}} \cM_{\cA^!}$
 computes $K_\tau(\cA, \cA^!)$
 (this is the formal content of the ambient complementarity
 construction: the derived fiber product of the two one-sided
 deformation problems is the twisted tensor product).
 Discreteness (virtual dimension~$0$) gives acyclicity of
 $K_\tau$, which is Koszulness
 (Definition~\ref{def:chiral-koszul-morphism}).
\end{itemize}
This step uses the ordinary twisted-tensor-product interpretation on
the Koszul surface. Off that surface, the file proves only the
intrinsic coderived/contraderived bar-coalgebra comparison of
Theorem~\ref{thm:positselski-chiral-proved}.

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{Standard-landscape verification.}
Hypotheses (P1)--(P3) are satisfied by every listed family.
(P\ref{item:perf-fingen}): all standard families have
positive-energy grading with finite-dimensional weight spaces.
(P\ref{item:perf-nondeg}): the invariant form is the Killing
form (nondegenerate at $k \neq -h^\vee$ for Kac--Moody), the
Shapovalov form (nondegenerate at generic~$c$ for Virasoro),
or the canonical pairing for free fields.
(P\ref{item:perf-dual}): Koszul duality preserves the positive-energy
grading and finite-dimensionality of weight spaces; the dual
pairing inherits nondegeneracy from the original.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scope and degeneration locus]
\label{rem:lagrangian-degeneration-locus}
The Lagrangian criterion degenerates precisely where the invariant
form degenerates: at the critical level $k = -h^\vee$ for
Kac--Moody, and at central charges where the Kac determinant
$\det G_h(c)$ vanishes (admissible levels for Virasoro).
At these points, the cyclic pairing develops a kernel and
perfectness fails, so the formal moduli problem
$\cM_{\mathrm{comp}}$ may not carry a well-defined
$(-1)$-shifted symplectic structure. This degeneration locus
is the same locus where the Shapovalov form degenerates
